<Text>It's a large investment to buy a solar system for your house.  That is why I spent time investigating the variables and the questions to ask before selecting a company.  There's a lot of good information online (i.e. energysage) and your friends and neighbors also have some great advice on questions to ask up front.  I assembled about 20 questions dealing with warranty, materials used, installation, experience, certifications, etc. and sent my questions to a few solar companies. The sales manager at ESP sent me back a curt message saying they would pass on the project.  What?  I asked what the problem was and he proceeded to tell me that it wasn't in their process to answer such questions up front.  Apparently questions about what materials they use and their efficiency, the warranty and such was too much "in the weeds" for them.  It boiled down to them assuming that if a prospect asks questions (really, pretty easy questions) that they will be hard to work with and the company doesn't want their business.  This manager said that asking detailed (and general) questions up front represented a "classic red flag" warning.  This is THE MOST BIZARRE thing I have ever dealt with in my life!  It certainly implies that they are hiding something and don't want you to compare with others.  He went on to say that these 20 questions represented a preview of more questions that I may have along the way that will "get in the way of us doing our jobs". < Text>
Came here on a gloomy Sunday morning and the line wasn't too long. Maybe it was because the rain was off and on that day, but the wait wasn't long at all. Small joint on a nice quiet street in SOMA.

Got a small table at the back near the kitchen. It didn't bother me since the restaurant is small to begin with and any spot inside will work. Note: If you have a party bigger than 3 or 4, this place is not for you. Think small restaurant with small tables.

We  ordered the eggs benedict with salmon and waffles. The food was excellent and it's a good local spot. If you're in the area, it's worth checking out but I wouldn't make a trek out just to try this place.<//Text>

< review>
This is the ideal French bistro weekend brunch spot. We found it to be extremely busy during the Saturday lunch hour; luckily, we waited for maybe about 25 minutes before our name was called on the list. Not too bad. We were seated near the front of the bistro (I believe there is an outdoor seating area near the back of the bistro). The place felt like a renovated home turned bistro. Lots of quirky old french posters hanging on the yellow painted walls. Each menu had a different front french poster cover. We liked their mimosas. I have to be honest, we had a hard time deciding on what to order...Oh, what to order!? There were so many excellent options to choose from! If you are vegetarian you'll be happy to find some options here. We decided on the Niman Ranch ham eggs benedict and the chicken dijon buckwheat pancakes to taste/share. Both of these savory dishes were tasty in their own right but I actually preferred the eggs Benedict over the buckwheat pancakes with chicken. Each dish was served with a side salad drizzled with a special light vinaigrette. I think what touched me the most was at the very end of our dining experience when we received our bill: complementary truffles accompanied the bill.</review>

<Text>The Butler & The Chef is quickly becoming one of my favorite places for brunch on Sundays.  A small place in South Park, you get a feeling that you have found a hidden treasure in the city.  It appears to be very small from the front, but has quite a few tables inside.  I've never seen an empty table to the two times I went for sunday brunch (it was also raining on those days).  There is typically a wait, but the turn around is pretty quick.

As for the food...Everything is made exceptionally well and very well portioned.  It is a bit pricey for brunch, but not pricey enough to detract from the food.  So far my favorite items have been the Eggs Benedict, the French Onion Soup Gratinee, and the Banana Belgium Waffle.

Great place to recover on sunday!  Only if they had bottomless mimosas....< /Text></record>

< Text>
Bizarre and unfriendly staff.

This USED to be our regular brunch place when we were in SOMA. My wife works nearby and stops in once or twice a month as a treat to pick up a croissant and a coffee. Today though, they decide that there's just no more pastries to go.

You want 6 croque monsieurs out the door? No problem. Cup of coffee?? That's fine. Scone? No way!! How dare you even ask?

You'd wonder why they'd keep all their pastries in a display case next to the register along with a stack of to go bags if you weren't supposed to... you know... buy them.

It's not hard people. You have food, we buy it. It's a long-standing and well respected formula for running a cafe. I guess you don't get it though. To be fair, I guess I understand. Who ever heard of a place that would actually sell customers coffee and a pastry and LET THEM WALK OUT THE DOOR WITH IT? That's crazy talk. Will never work. Don't tell John Q. Starbucks, his ideas are just too crazy.

Seriously Butler & Chef, go suck a lemon. Not everyone can spend an hour on a weekday luxuriating in your cute little bistro. Sometimes its nice though to do your part to spread a little morning cheer.< /Text>

<userid>102339263831305186460< /userid>< Name>
Cloud King< /Name>
< Time>
1498173039675</Time>
< rate>
4< /rate>
< text>
This place is beautiful. It has a separate day use area away from the overnight camping area. The bathrooms are clean and include showers, and have been redone after the flood.

As for water access, in the day use area there is everything from a small trickling brook, to a small, slow moving river that is somewhat warm in the shallows and a bit colder in the deeper parts. It has a ramp where you can launch canoes and other small water craft. From there it's a short walk to the fast moving, and very cold, Yuba River where the scenery is breathtaking.

There is a wide open area for groups to gather, as the Cherokee do anually, a pavilion, and plenty of woods to explore. Near the river is a covered area with plenty of tables that can be reserved for parties. There are also many other tables and benches scattered around the area for singles or single families.

One thing Sycamore Ranch is not short on is wild animals. From birds such as; Heron, Raven, Turkeys, and Vultures; to woodland creatures like Squirrels; to Frogs, Fish, and many others. You will enjoy catching site of each one.

The overnight camping side has many large sites with plenty of trees for shade. There is a larger launching area here that goes straight into the Yuba River.

I go to this place as often as I can and, since the day use area is free and open from 1/2 hour after sunrise to 1/2 hour before sunset, that is often! I hope you come join me in the beauty of this natural wonder, and please help me keep it clean for us all to enjoy.< /text>

< Review>
This was by far the best of the three places I visited looking for a Rolex. No doubt it will be my first stop if I am looking for another watch. Jill and Markus were excellent. They answered all my questions, were patient while I looked at watches and seemed to genuinely want to help find the watch I would be happy with.

There was one watch in stock that I was interested in. They let me try it on a couple times, and patiently waited as I considered it and asked questions that came to mind. The watch was 34mm and not 36mm like I was originally looking for. They pulled up a picture of the larger watch to show me the difference in the dial between the sizes and let me try on a similar watch in 36mm so I could get an idea of the size and feel. I actually prefer the dial style of the smaller watch and I have slender wrists so it doesn't look too small on me.

We talked about how it would work if I wanted to get the larger size or different model. They didn't push or try to persuade me to purchase the watch in stock over waiting for a different one. I told them I was going to think about it and left to get some food.

After eating I went to back to take another look and decided to buy the watch. We took care of payment, registration and fitting the watch. I didn't sense any rush and it wasn't until they unlocked the door to let me out that I realized it was well passed their closing time.

If you are looking for a watch or other jewelry I would recommend checking out Heller Jewelers.</Review>

<user>105322962280889066183</user><pictures>None<//pictures><Response>{'time': 1544471113361, 'text': 'Thank you for your kind words and review Marco. We loved working to find your perfect timepiece and look forward to seeing you in store again soon.'}< /Response>< review>
When I turned 30 this year, I developed a passion for horology and watches. I also just retired and moved on from one passionate hobby (sneaker) and found myself graduated to another, more expensive one in watches.

As my first watches, I bought myself an Omega Speedmaster FOIS and Tag Heuer Carrera 41. My Tag needed to be resized so I looked for the nearest Tag AD. I came across Heller's Jewelers here on Yelp and saw they were in San Ramon. Although they were 30 min away, I noticed that they had one of the best reviews for customer service on Google and Yelp. Since customer service is my #1 focus, I gave this place a call.

Markus answered the phone. I asked him what the fee was for resizing my Tag and he told me he would do it free of charge. I was quite surprised as other places would charge. Full disclosure: I did buy my Tag from the official boutique store and not from the grey market. Coincidentally, I was searching for a reputable Rolex AD to build a loyal relationship with and purchase my first Rolex. Heller's Jewelers is a Rolex AD, so I figured I'll make the trip to San Ramon from Pittsburg.

When I arrived, I was pleasantly greeted by Markus. He resized my Tag and offered me water while I waited. The conversation was surprisingly genuine and enlightening, especially since I didn't buy anything! After he finished resizing, I decided to inquire about their Rolex inventory. I described to Markus what I was seeking, and he helped me find a Datejust 41, white dial, smooth bezel and oystersteel bracelet. Markus walked me through the entire process, educated me, and provided me with multiple options with no pressure. His consultation personally made it a first class experience for me. I then put in the order, and not only did it came earlier than I expected, but Markus made accommodations for me as well.

When I finally picked up my Datejust, the experience was fabulous. My girlfriend and I were offered champagne, beer, coffee, water and etc, a Rolex experience that I expected and was delighted from. I saw my watch unboxed and tried it on. Markus made this experience very memorable for me as I celebrate a big milestone I achieved as well as obtain my first Rolex. I will always be thankful to Markus for respecting my moment, making it more special.

I am currently looking at engagement rings and will definitely be working with Marcus!

If you're looking for a jeweler who you want to build a long lasting relationship and experience outstanding customer service, then give Heller's a call. That's what I did, and ever since then, I never looked anywhere else.<//review>

I have been going to Hellers Jewelry for the past 5 years for all my Rolex needs. The staff is very friendly and knowledgeable about  the watches. They never pushed or rushed me to buy.
